  <span id="freeText11451412845505401856" style="display:none">Dear Author Tom Rob Smith......Seriously? That's the ending you're going with? <br /><br />This book was starting out to be one of my favorite books of all time! It was quite brilliant and written perfectly. I couldn't wait to read a word, a page, anything - picking it up at red lights, while curling my hair, brushing my teeth or cooking dinner. I was intrigued and excited, I couldn't wait to turn the page. <br /><br />The beginning pulled me in and I was lost in he world of Sweden and the lives of Tilde, Daniel and Chris. Tilde's story was so compelling and I went back &amp; forth between believing &amp; questioning her. What a story she told....sex, drugs, lies and murder! Creepy wooden troll dolls and intimidating Sweden farmers, hidden doors &amp; locked rooms. Wow! Exciting, engaging. I couldn't put the book down. <br /><br />Absolutely brilliant, wonderful, exciting, intriguing......until you betrayed me, stabbed me in the back! I feel as I was on a high speed chase, just to lose the criminal; on the verge of an orgasm, just as someone knocks on the door; digging into a lavish meal, just to taste nothing. <br /><br />Tom Rob Smith- Did you just run out of creative ideas? Rushed for an ending to meet your publisher's demands? The characters that you spent so much time building and constructing turned out to be.........nothing, unimportant and bland. <br /><br />I'm sad, depressed, angry and so very disappointed. I am giving this book two stars because the writing is perfectly crafted and most of the book is brilliant. I wish I could give it more, but the betrayal is so deep that I will finish this review and never speak of The Farm again. </span>

        <a title="Dimitris Passas (TapTheLine)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dimitris Passas (TapTheLine)" href="/user/show/19705183-dimitris-passas-taptheline">Dimitris Passas (TapTheLine)</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2640945554" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17410162274436296972">''The Farm'' is a crime/mystery novel, written by Tom Rob Smith (''Child 44'', ''London Spy'', ''American Crime Story'') and it is a book I finished in one day (two sittings), something that rarely happens to me. I was immediately drawn to the story which begins when Daniel, being one of the two protagonists/narrators and living in London, gets a call from his father (Chris) who has recently moved permanently to Sweden with his wife, on an isolated farm somewhere in the <br/>countryside. Chris says t</span>
  <span id="freeText17410162274436296972" style="display:none">''The Farm'' is a crime/mystery novel, written by Tom Rob Smith (''Child 44'', ''London Spy'', ''American Crime Story'') and it is a book I finished in one day (two sittings), something that rarely happens to me. I was immediately drawn to the story which begins when Daniel, being one of the two protagonists/narrators and living in London, gets a call from his father (Chris) who has recently moved permanently to Sweden with his wife, on an isolated farm somewhere in the <br />countryside. Chris says to Daniel that his dear mother is committed to a mental clinic after a psychotic breakdown, full of paranoid delusions and having no connection with the reality anymore. The mother, Tilde, manages to get out of the hospital and takes the plane in order to meet Daniel and tell him her side of the story, about a massive conspiracy in which her husband and Daniel's father is involved, along with many other residents of the small village that she is now living. Daniel will have to listen carefully his mother's account and try to discern the truth in her story, if there is any, and then decide what he is going to do. Take his mother to the hospital or to the police station to tell the authorities her story? Is she a reliable or an unreliable narrator? <br />The first half of the novel is about Tilde's narration of the strange events that started happening when she and Chris moved to Sweden, which if properly combined, shape a larger picture that reveals a grim reality of corruption, xenophobia and -possibly- murder in the small community. In the second part we read about Daniel's journey to Sweden in order to find himself the truth about his mother's accusations. The finale is dignified, with a nice plot twist, and acts as the best ending to a compelling and suspenseful plot.<br />Tom Rob Smith's prose is simple, without being simplistic, and immediate so the reader keeps turning the pages in this rather long novel (more than 400 pages) which can be read even in one sitting. It will mainly appeal to the fans of literary and crime fiction as well as to anyone who enjoys a well-narrated mystery story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17410162274436296972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_859166497" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/859166497" />
    <a title="Blair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/272909-blair"><img alt="Blair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493499323p2/272909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/859166497?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blair" href="/user/show/272909-blair">Blair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19747243-the-farm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=2014-release">2014-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=mystery-thriller-etc">mystery-thriller-etc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer859166497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer193965604427276401"><i>The Farm</i> presents itself as a taut, gripping thriller in which a man is torn between different stories told to him by his parents. Daniel's father claims his mother is not of sound mind, while she insists she has uncovered a terrible conspiracy surrounding their new home, an isolated farm in Sweden. Most of the narrative is given over to the mother's - Tilde's - story, as heard by Daniel; he interjects occasionally, but on the whole this is a very traditional, chronological account of events. On</span>
  <span id="freeText193965604427276401" style="display:none"><i>The Farm</i> presents itself as a taut, gripping thriller in which a man is torn between different stories told to him by his parents. Daniel's father claims his mother is not of sound mind, while she insists she has uncovered a terrible conspiracy surrounding their new home, an isolated farm in Sweden. Most of the narrative is given over to the mother's - Tilde's - story, as heard by Daniel; he interjects occasionally, but on the whole this is a very traditional, chronological account of events. Only in the very last part of the novel does Daniel take matters into his own hands, travelling to Sweden in the hope of establishing the truth.<br /> <br />The story grabs your attention immediately, and it's all very fast-paced, so this is an easy read. But honestly, I'm starting to think twists and secrets are becoming a bit of a scourge on contemporary fiction and particularly thrillers. I knew there had to be something wrong here, otherwise there would be no source of tension: the reader is invited to decide whether they believe Tilde or not, but there's no counter-argument to dispute her account, so the narrative isn't exactly fairly weighted. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It was too obvious that the twist had to be either that a) Tilde actually was mad or b) she was partly right, but had got some details wrong, and embellished others. What drama would there have been at the end if she had been right all along? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> <br />That said, there are a lot of interesting themes in <i>The Farm</i>, to do with creating and telling stories; the importance of these as 'truths' (especially within families); the lies we tell our parents (and vice versa); the similar perception of stories told/memories recalled in both youth and old age as untrustworthy. I think you have to think deeply about the book to actually see them, though. It's a clever thing to make the story deceptively multi-layered, but it reads as almost too straightforward on the surface.<br /> <br />I think I tried to read one of the author's historical thrillers once and was totally uninterested in it, so this was definitely an improvement, but I didn't find it very memorable. It was just alright.</span>
  <a data-text-id="193965604427276401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18335772-marnie?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18335772-marnie?shelf=published-in-2014">published-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18335772-marnie?shelf=atw-sweden">atw-sweden</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18335772-marnie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer956522639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6576122023720544966">First off- this is not <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2161733.Child_44__Leo_Demidov___1_' title='Child 44 (Leo Demidov, #1) by Tom Rob Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Child 44</a>. This is not an action/ thriller so if that is what you are looking for - select another book. This is a mystery. <br/><br/>Daniel gets a phone call from his father that his mother has gone crazy and has been institutionalized ( hello 1800's ). Rushing to the airport Daniel gets a call from his mother that she has escaped Sweden and that his father and others are out to "get" her. Who to believe? Is the mother a victim or an unreliable narrator? That is the mystery.<br/><br/>The auth</span>
  <span id="freeText6576122023720544966" style="display:none">First off- this is not <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2161733.Child_44__Leo_Demidov___1_" title="Child 44 (Leo Demidov, #1) by Tom Rob Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">Child 44</a>. This is not an action/ thriller so if that is what you are looking for - select another book. This is a mystery. <br /><br />Daniel gets a phone call from his father that his mother has gone crazy and has been institutionalized ( hello 1800's ). Rushing to the airport Daniel gets a call from his mother that she has escaped Sweden and that his father and others are out to "get" her. Who to believe? Is the mother a victim or an unreliable narrator? That is the mystery.<br /><br />The author did do a great job setting the scene. My favorite quote in describing the desolate farm in Sweden: <br />"...as isolation sinks into our consciousness we change, not at first but slowly....It alters our notion of how we should behave, of what is acceptable, and, most important of all, what we can get away with."<br /><br />My biggest drawback was the telling of events in past tense which took away all the suspense and I never had a sense of danger. At first I enjoyed the slow unravelling of the story but after 150 pages or so I found it a tad frustrating. <br />It was an interesting story but not as compelling as the other book by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/981834.Tom_Rob_Smith" title="Tom Rob Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">Tom Rob Smith</a> that I have read.</span>

<div id="review_3330169253" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3330169253" />
    <a title="Chris Steeden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21637893-chris-steeden"><img alt="Chris Steeden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472139374p2/21637893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3330169253?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Steeden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Steeden" href="/user/show/21637893-chris-steeden">Chris Steeden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20030784-the-farm">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3330169253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8496590700797264169">A terrible crime has been committed on a Swedish farm. Or has it? That is the premise of Tom Rob Smith’s novel. The author is of Child 44 fame and has written a rather compelling book here.<br/><br/>Set in rural Sweden and London. We follow Mark who is a rooftop garden designer in London. His parents have retired to a farm in Sweden. His mother, Tilde, is Swedish. She had left home at the age of 16 and moved to England. She has her secrets. Mark has a secret as well which he has kept from his parents. His</span>
  <span id="freeText8496590700797264169" style="display:none">A terrible crime has been committed on a Swedish farm. Or has it? That is the premise of Tom Rob Smith’s novel. The author is of Child 44 fame and has written a rather compelling book here.<br /><br />Set in rural Sweden and London. We follow Mark who is a rooftop garden designer in London. His parents have retired to a farm in Sweden. His mother, Tilde, is Swedish. She had left home at the age of 16 and moved to England. She has her secrets. Mark has a secret as well which he has kept from his parents. His parents, together, also have a secret which they have kept from Mark.<br /><br />Once more Tilde has run away from Sweden but why? The past and the present constantly mixing. She tells Mark the whole story. I was absolutely hooked on Tilde’s story. Is it true? Is she mad? What is going on? The book is fast paced but do not expect it to be like Child 44. It is not. The atmosphere can, at times, be damn right creepy and you are certainly put on edge. <br /><br />OK, so for the ending. Is it an anti-climax like a lot of reviewers have noted? Well, it is rather. This could have been a five-star book for me. Nevertheless, I enjoyed it immensely.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8496590700797264169" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_959695520" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/959695520" />
    <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes"><img alt="Nancy Oakes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507555979p2/900340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/959695520?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy Oakes" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes">Nancy Oakes</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780446550734" href="/book/show/18656067-the-farm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/900340-nancy-oakes?shelf=uk-fiction">uk-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer959695520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18073488200820388691">I liked this one. <br/><br/>for a longer look at this novel, feel free to click on over to my <a href='http://www.readingavidly.com/2014/07/just-another-month-of-summer-left-dont.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>online reading journal</a>; otherwise, this is the short version.<br/><br/>The Farm is a multilayered story within a story within a story that is slowly peeled back like the proverbial onion until you reach its core. The opening sequence is a total grabber. The narrator, Daniel, receives a call from his dad Chris telling him that his mom Tilde is sick, that she's been "imagining things -- terrible, terrible things," and that s</span>
  <span id="freeText18073488200820388691" style="display:none">I liked this one. <br /><br />for a longer look at this novel, feel free to click on over to my <a href="http://www.readingavidly.com/2014/07/just-another-month-of-summer-left-dont.html" rel="nofollow noopener">online reading journal</a>; otherwise, this is the short version.<br /><br />The Farm is a multilayered story within a story within a story that is slowly peeled back like the proverbial onion until you reach its core. The opening sequence is a total grabber. The narrator, Daniel, receives a call from his dad Chris telling him that his mom Tilde is sick, that she's been "imagining things -- terrible, terrible things," and that she's been sick all summer. Now she seems to be "suffering from a psychotic episode," and is now voluntarily committed. As Daniel gets ready to make the trip from London to Sweden, his father calls him again to tell him that there's a problem -- Tilde, it seems, is not there; she's evidently convinced the doctors to let her go and now Chris has no clue where she may be. He does inform his son that he is among the people Tilde's been making accusations against, and that "none of what she claims is real." While Chris rings off to check their joint bank account, Daniel gets a call from his mother saying that she'll be landing in London in just two hours and that<br /><br />"Everything that man has told you is a lie. I'm not mad. I don't need a doctor. I need the police."<br /><br />From there, Tilde and Daniel sit for hours and hours while she goes through a satchel filled with what she calls evidence of her husband's involvement in a horrible criminal conspiracy. The story she tells reveals much to Daniel about herself and her husband, and by the time the story reaches its conclusion, Daniel comes to realize a lot about himself as well. <br /><br />The Farm is a twisty novel, one that really plays heavily on reader expectations. The reader, up to a point, takes the same position as Daniel here, that of both judge and jury, having to decide whether or not Tilde's version of things is true and his dad is guilty of terrible crimes, or whether she really does need to be back in a hospital receiving treatment. In the meantime he begins to realize that there are a number of things about his parents he never knew, leading to the idea that maybe we don't know people as well as we think we do. <br /><br />This is another one of those books where I had to take time to let things come together in my head, but I have to say, I ended up liking it. While there are some spots where the pace seems sort of sluggish, each time Tilde took something out of her satchel things started to heat up again and I was drawn back in and ready for whatever might happen next. The ending comes fast, sort of out of proportion to the big buildup that proceeded it, but it is a bit of a shocker. It also hit home the idea that as much as you may want to ignore the past, sometimes it might be better to confront it. I also felt that since Daniel has such a weight on his shoulders here, he might have shown as much energy throughout the story as he did toward the end, but in the long run, The Farm is a really good summer read that will leave you thinking about those closest to you and the secrets they carry. It's also a heck of a ride.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18073488200820388691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_823867495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/823867495" />
    <a title="Shelleyrae at Book&#39;d Out" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1607230-shelleyrae-at-book-d-out"><img alt="Shelleyrae at Book&#39;d Out" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328852907p2/1607230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/823867495?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelleyrae at Book&#39;d Out" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelleyrae at Book&#39;d Out" href="/user/show/1607230-shelleyrae-at-book-d-out">Shelleyrae at Book&#39;d Out</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781847375704" href="/book/show/20551609-the-farm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1607230-shelleyrae-at-book-d-out?shelf=provided-by-publisher">provided-by-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1607230-shelleyrae-at-book-d-out?shelf=arc-are">arc-are</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer823867495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5171510512435720864"><br/>"Promise that you'll listen to everything I say with an open mind. All I ask for is an open mind. Promise me you'll do that, that's why I've come to you. Promise me!"<br/><br/>Daniel is shocked when his father rings in tears to announce his mother is sick, not physically ill but mentally, and he has been forced to admit her to a psychiatric hospital. Distraught, Daniel makes immediate plans to travel to Sweden where his parents now live, but before he can board the plane his mother arrives in London, clut</span>
  <span id="freeText5171510512435720864" style="display:none"><br />"Promise that you'll listen to everything I say with an open mind. All I ask for is an open mind. Promise me you'll do that, that's why I've come to you. Promise me!"<br /><br />Daniel is shocked when his father rings in tears to announce his mother is sick, not physically ill but mentally, and he has been forced to admit her to a psychiatric hospital. Distraught, Daniel makes immediate plans to travel to Sweden where his parents now live, but before he can board the plane his mother arrives in London, clutching a battered satchel claiming that his father is conspiring against her. Demanding that Daniel listen, his mother begins to speak, asking Daniel to trust in her tale of secrets, lies, betrayal, corruption and perversion. Daniel doesn't know who to believe, he can't imagine either of his quiet, hard working, loving parents capable of deception but he has to know...just who is telling the truth?<br /><br />The Farm is a psychological thriller where Smith unravels a finely crafted plot that examines the issues of trust, truth and betrayal. The story unfolds from the perspective of Daniel and Tilde, his mother, as she shares a tale with him, exposing her belief in a conspiracy that implicates the residents of a small Swedish community, and his father, in a shocking crime.<br /><br />"I'm sure your father has spoken to you. Everything that man has told you is a lie. I'm not mad."<br /><br />Daniel has never had any reason to distrust either of his parents but as his mother speaks he realises he has been oblivious to his parents lives, underscored by his surprise at the financial crisis that forced his parents move to Sweden. With the awareness that both his parents are capable of lying to him, Daniel is torn, unable to conclusively determine who is telling the truth. While his mother's story seems outlandish and his father appears genuinely distressed, the uncertainty nags at him and he decides the only way to determine the truth is to investigate his mother's claims himself.<br /><br />With consummate skill, Smith keeps the reader guessing, unable to completely dismiss, or fully believe in, Tilde's conspiracy theory. The author fosters an atmosphere of unease and tension as the reader wonders whose side should they take, and what if it's the wrong one? The plot is masterful and the characterisation well done, but I have to confess there was something about the author's style that didn't quite grab me, and I was unable to completely lose myself in the novel. Nevertheless, I did like The Farm, particularly admiring its original premise, and I would recommend it without hesitation.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5171510512435720864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_830126760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/830126760" />
    <a title="Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4986986-tracey-allen-at-carpe-librum"><img alt="Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459779189p2/4986986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/830126760?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum" href="/user/show/4986986-tracey-allen-at-carpe-librum">Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781847375698" href="/book/show/18310839-the-farm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4986986-tracey-allen-at-carpe-librum?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4986986-tracey-allen-at-carpe-librum?shelf=signed-by-author">signed-by-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer830126760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4780159697905129564">Oh my goodness! I've been hanging out to read <i>The Farm</i> by Tom Rob Smith ever since I heard the premise:<br/>Daniel's parents have retired to Sweden, and all seems well until he receives a call from his father.<br/><i>"Your mother's not well. She's been imagining things - terrible, terrible things. She's had a psychotic breakdown, and has been committed to a mental hospital." </i><br/><br/>But then his mother rings to say: <i>"I'm sure your father has spoken to you. Everything that man has told you is a lie. I'm not mad. I do</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4780159697905129564" style="display:none">Oh my goodness! I've been hanging out to read <i>The Farm</i> by Tom Rob Smith ever since I heard the premise:<br />Daniel's parents have retired to Sweden, and all seems well until he receives a call from his father.<br /><i>"Your mother's not well. She's been imagining things - terrible, terrible things. She's had a psychotic breakdown, and has been committed to a mental hospital." </i><br /><br />But then his mother rings to say: <i>"I'm sure your father has spoken to you. Everything that man has told you is a lie. I'm not mad. I don't need a doctor. I need the police. I'm about to board a flight to London. Meet me at Heathrow." </i> (Source: GoodReads).<br /><br />Daniel then has to decide which of his parents to believe. I was instantly hooked by the premise, and instantly gripped by the plot as soon as I picked up the book.<br /><br />In fact, there was so much tension in <i>The Farm</i>, that I actually exclaimed, out loud, twice! The first was when Daniel's Mum says the simple words: "I told him everything" and I instantly yelled out "NO!"<br /><br />And the second was when it was clear Daniel had made his decision about which parent to believe (no spoilers though). Oh, and the ending too, so I guess that makes three out loud exclamations and luckily for me they all occurred at home.<br /><br /><i>The Farm</i> is a mystery and psychological thriller, which is surprising given the content is not driven by action so much as learning the truth about what took place. The plot is tight and the tension is palpable, and I thoroughly enjoyed it and highly recommend it. <br /><br />I was also pleased to learn the movie rights have been sold, hopefully it's not too long before we can watch <i>The Farm</i> on the big screen. Get it, read it now!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4780159697905129564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('q0fla8EluB1YUwW/sX2wnwwVymQZKFbdxWQp5DOFSZdRdUB9A3h8GudUd2ZxZUVdSsgHKTvYV3C2wfoxoxxWBQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('S2dHbDp3Dwam6r1z2cezfmJ2Q8cLczDOEXAw5xCl6gSxVeJ6+CrLARntz6oZ30a8JKuOiimDMWNi1eMygDz1lg==')})
  }

But it was clear - to some - that the Soviet Union was already executing a plan to expand and foment revolution around the world. The American government\'s strategy in response relied on the secret efforts of a newly-formed CIA.\n\nThe Quiet Americans chronicles the exploits of four spies - Michael Burke, a charming former football star fallen on hard times, Frank Wisner, the scion of a wealthy Southern family, Peter Sichel, a sophisticated German Jew who escaped the Nazis, and Edward Lansdale, a brilliant ad executive. The four ran covert operations across the globe, trying to outwit the ruthless KGB in Berlin, parachuting commandos into Eastern Europe, plotting coups, and directing wars against Communist insurgents in Asia.\n\nBut time and again their efforts went awry, thwarted by a combination of stupidity and ideological rigidity at the highest levels of the government - and more profoundly, the decision to abandon American ideals. By the mid-1950s, the Soviet Union had a stranglehold on Eastern Europe, the U.S. had begun its disastrous intervention in Vietnam, and America, the beacon of democracy, was overthrowing democratically-elected governments and earning the hatred of much of the world. All of this culminated in an act of betrayal and cowardice that would lock the Cold War into place for decades to come.\n\nAnderson brings to the telling of this story all the narrative brio, deep research, skeptical eye, and lively prose that made Lawrence in Arabia a major international bestseller. The intertwined lives of these men began in a common purpose of defending freedom, but the ravages of the Cold War led them to different fates. Two would quit the CIA in despair, stricken by the moral compromises they had to make; one became the archetype of the duplicitous and destructive American spy; and one would be so heartbroken he would take his own life.\n\nThe Quiet Americans is the story of these four men. It is also the story of how the United States, at the very pinnacle of its power, managed to snatch defeat from the jaws of victory.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2648460333901730102\" href=\"#\" This decisive period in Chinese history became a subject of intense and continuing inter<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText10644395837034433149\" style=\"display:none\">Three Kingdoms tells the story of the fateful last reign of the Han dynasty (206 B.C.-A.D. 220), when the Chinese empire was divided into three warring kingdoms. This decisive period in Chinese history became a subject of intense and continuing interest to historians, poets, and dramatists. Writing some 1,200 years later, the Ming author Luo Guanzhong drew on this rich literary heritage to fashion a sophisticated, compelling narrative that has become the Chinese national epic. Luo\'s novel offers a startling and unsparing view of how power is wielded, how diplomacy is conducted, and how wars are planned and fought; it has influenced the ways the Chinese think about power, diplomacy, and war even to this day. As important for Chinese culture as the Homeric epics have been for the West, this Ming dynasty masterpiece continues to be widely influential in China, Japan, Korea, and Vietnam, and remains a great work of world literature.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/981834.Tom_Rob_Smith">About Tom Rob Smith</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/981834.Tom_Rob_Smith"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1254868572p3/981834.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer274751992124856757">Tom Rob Smith (born 1979) is an English writer. The son of a Swedish mother and an English father, Smith was raised in London where he lives today. After graduating from Cambridge University in 2001, he completed his studies in Italy, studying creative writing for a year. After these studies, he worked as a scriptwriter.<br/><br/>His first novel, Child 44, about a series of child murders in Stalinist Russia</span>
  <span id="freeText274751992124856757" style="display:none">Tom Rob Smith (born 1979) is an English writer. The son of a Swedish mother and an English father, Smith was raised in London where he lives today. After graduating from Cambridge University in 2001, he completed his studies in Italy, studying creative writing for a year. After these studies, he worked as a scriptwriter.<br /><br />His first novel, Child 44, about a series of child murders in Stalinist Russia, appeared in early 2008 and was translated into 17 languages. It was awarded the 2008 Ian Fleming Steel Dagger for Best Thriller of the year by the Crime Writer's Association. It was recently a Barnes &amp; Noble recommended book. On July 29, 2008 the book was named on the long list for the 2008 Man Booker Prize. In November 2008, he was nominated for the 2008 Costa First Novel Award (former Whitbread).<br /><br />Child 44 followed-up by The Secret Speech (2009)and Agent 6 (2011).<br /><br />Japanese: トム ロブ スミス </span>
  <a data-text-id="274751992124856757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
